treasury is also translated as the space treasure – it  refers to the fact that bodhisattvas will be able 
to provided whatever sentient beings n eed, be it  wealth or enjoyments.   
 Poverty also refers to real poverty like having no thing to eat and no place to sleep.  It is clearly 
mentioned in the commentary that when we talk about the sky treasury, we can provide sentient 
beings not only with the objects of enjoymen t that they need but also  with Dharma.  
 
[3,30] 
It is the supreme medicine 
That quells the world’s disease. 
It is the tree that shelters all beings 
Wandering and tired on the path of conditioned existence 
3B2B 2A2A 3A2A 3 Destroying disease 
This is explained in the first two lines in verse 30: “It is the supreme medicine that quells the 
world’s disease.” When we talk about disease, we are referring to the actual physical diseases and 
also the diseases of the mind. The bodhicitta is  the supreme medicine that eliminates all these 
diseases. How is bodhicitta able to eliminate natural diseases?  
 According to Tibetan medicine, all our illnesse s can be classified into one of these three 
categories: wind, bile and phlegm. The roots of these three diseases are the mental poisons. 
According to Tibetan medicine, our afflictions gi ve rise to these three kinds of diseases.  
Bodhicitta  can cut or destroy these three mental  poisons. Once we destroy the cause, we will 
have no effect. No cause,  therefore no disease.  When we destroy the th ree mental poisons, we 
can overcome the actual diseases of the body. That is why we say bodh icitta is the supreme 
medicine for all diseases.  
3B2B 2A2A 3A2A 4 Destroying in general the sufferings of samsara 
Bodhicitta also destroys the sufferings of samsara or  cyclic existence itself as shown in the last two 
lines of verse 30: “It is the tree that shelters all beings wandering and tired on the path of 
conditioned existence”. Bodhicitta is like the tr ee that shelters all beings who are wandering and 
tired on the path of conditioned existence (ie wandering in cyclic existence). It is mentioned in 
the treatises that bodhisattvas must be trained in  the paths of the hearer  and solitary realiser 
besides training in the Mahayana path. This is to benefit the people of that lineage. Bodhisattvas 
must train in that path to lead sentient bein gs to the state of liberation. According to the 
individual disposition or the fortun e of the trainees/disciples belonging  to the hearer or solitary 
realiser lineages and in order to benefit th em, bodhisattvas teach and help them to free 
Amitabha Buddhist Centre       Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds 
F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m              C h a p t e r  T h r e e  
 
 
148 themselves temporarily  from suffering by placing th em in the state of liberation. It is bodhicitta 
that enables bodhisattvas to do this. It is due to  the power of bodhicitta that  bodhisattvas are 
able to help sentient beings free th emselves from cyclic existence.  
 
[3, 31] 
It is the universal bridge 
That leads to freedom from unhappy states of birth, 
It is the dawning moon of the mind 
That dispels the torment of  disturbing conceptions. 
3B2B 2A2A 3A2A 5 Destroying specifically the sufferings of the lower realms 
This is shown in the first two lines of verse 31: “It is the universal bridge that leads to freedom 
from unhappy states of birth.” Bodhisattvas are ab le to show sentient beings what are the things 
to be abandoned and what are the things to be cultivated. By showing them the teachings 
correctly, this helps sentient beings, in the short te rm, to gain higher rebirths and not to fall into 
the lower realms. Bodhisattvas are able to do this  because of bodhicitta. Bodhicitta is like the 
universal bridge that supports and leads sentient beings to freedom from the lower realms. This 
is because bodhisattvas are able to teach sentient  beings the method to avoid going to the lower 
realms. Bodhisattvas also teach sentient beings the method, in the short term, to achieve higher 
rebirths as human beings and gods. The path of ac hieving higher rebirths as humans and gods is 
the path shared with persons of all three differen t spiritual capacities. The universal bridge refers 
to the lives as human beings and gods. Since this is a good rebirth that comes from the power of 
bodhicitta, so bodhicitta is the universal bridge. 
3B2B 2A2A 3A2B  The potential [power] to dispel the obscurations - the causes [of suffering] 
1 Dispelling afflictive obscurations 
2 Dispelling the obscurations to knowledge 
 
Bodhicitta has the power to eliminate the tw o obscurations: afflictive obscurations and 
obscurations to knowledge. [Afflictive obscurations is also translated as ob structions to liberation. 
Obstructions to knowledge is also transl ated as obstructions to omniscience]. 
3B2B 2A2A 3A2B 1  Dispelling afflictive obscurations 
Bodhicitta has the power to elimin ate the afflictive obstructions. This is shown is the last two 
lines of verse 31: “It is the dawning moon of th e mind that dispels the torment of disturbing 
conceptions.” 
[3, 32] 
It is the great sun that finally removes 
The misty ignorance of the world, 
It is the quintessential butter 
From the churning of the milk of Dharma 
Amitabha Buddhist Centre       Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds 
F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m              C h a p t e r  T h r e e  
 
 
149 3B2B 2A2A 3A2B 2  Dispelling the obscurations to knowledge 
Bodhicitta has the power to destroy the obstructio ns to knowledge and as  shown in the 1st  two 
lines of verse 32: “It is the great sun that finally removes the misty ignorance of the world”. It says 
here that bodhicitta can eliminate the afflictions or negative emotions. Not only that. Bodhicitta 
can even eliminate completely the imprints or the predisposition of those afflictions or negative 
emotions. How does this happen? When we say ‘dis pel’ here, it is dispelling from the root.   
  Answer by a student:  Bodhicitta is  analogous to having great strength and  wisdom is like a sharp 
axe. The obstructions to omniscience is like a  tree. If we have weak arms, we cannot  lift up the sharp axe. Only with powerful arms and a sharp a x e  w i l l  w e   b e  a b l e  t o  c h o p  d o w n  t h e  t r e e .  
Bodhicitta is the strength that ma kes one able to lift up the very sharp axe. Bodhic itta creates the 
merit accumulated  from practising the six perfecti ons.  However we still need wisdom (the axe) 
to be able to cut the tree down. 
 According to the root text, bodhicitta is the da wning moon of the mind that dispels the torment 
or pain that the afflictions or negative emotio ns inflict on our minds. Such mental pain is 
brought about by the manifest afflictions. When ange r, pride or jealousy manifests, it causes pain 
in our minds. When we generate bodhicitta, it is  likened to the moon that completely outshines 
all these manifest afflictions. A ll the torments associated with th e afflictions will be removed.  
 One of the practices for developing bodhicitta is to train our minds by giving our bodies, wealth 
and possessions and our roots of virtue to sentient beings. Once we are able to do that, then we 
will be able to generate bodhicitta. When we ar e able to develop bodhici tta, we will not have any 
miserliness, anger, attachment or desire. We are re ferring here to the afflictions in their manifest 
form which  bodhicitta will be able to remove.    But it is difficult to say whether bodhicitta alone can eliminate the afflictions from the root. If we 
really want to completely remove afflictions fr om the root, then there is one way - one has to 
achieve  the wisdom that realises emptiness or self lessness. All the valid texts agree on this point. 
All the tenet systems agree  that we need the wi sdom that realises emptiness or selflessness to 
eliminate the afflictions and to uproot th e imprints of these negative emotions. 
  When the root text refers to bo dhicitta as the dawning moon of  the mind that can dispel the 
torment of afflictions, we have to understand that this refers to the manifest afflictions. 
Bodhicitta can eliminate manifest afflictions.  But bodhicitta alone cannot eliminate those 
negative emotions from their root. We need to have  the wisdom that realises  selflessness. That is 
a must. What about the imprints of those negative  e m o t i o n s  t h a t  w e  c a l l  t h e  o b s t r u c t i o n s  t o  
omniscience or obstructions to knowledge? What  is it that prevents someone from attaining 
omniscience? How do we  eliminat e the imprints of these obstruct ions? The text says bodhicitta 
can achieve this. By depending on wisdom alone, one will not be able to eliminate the imprints 
Amitabha Buddhist Centre       Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds 
F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m              C h a p t e r  T h r e e  
 
 
150 of those negative emotions.  
 
According to the highest tenet system, the Pr asangika-Madhyamika sc hool, the hearers and 
solitary realisers can achieve liberation through the wisdom that realises selflessness. Although 
the hearer arhats and solitary realiser pratyekabu ddhas are able to achieve liberation, they are not 
able to eliminate the imprints of their negative  emotions. Although they have abandoned their 
negative emotions from the root, they have not abandoned the root itself. Why? This is because 
they do not have the support of the vast accumu lation of merit that co mes from bodhicitta.  
 We have to be able to explain how bodhicitta ca n eliminate the obstructions to omniscience. We 
have to say that obstructions to  omniscience are removed by the wi sdom that realises selflessness 
that is  conjoined with the vast accumulation of  merit that comes from bodhicitta. We have to 
explain it in this way. The obstructions to omniscience are not abandoned on the first seven 
bodhisattva grounds. Once the bodhisattvas have  achieved the eighth ground, the bodhisattvas 
have abandoned all the afflictions or negative  afflictions from the root. The process of 
abandoning the obstructions to omniscience st arts from the eighth ground. On the eighth, 
nineth and tenth grounds, they require the accumu lation of vast amounts of merit in order to 
help them to  abandon completely the obstructions to omniscience.  
 Whether one is able to remove the obstructio ns to omniscience depends on whether one has 
bodhicitta or not. The bodhisattvas only start to abandon th e obstructions to omniscience from 
the 8th ground onwards but they have already ab andoned the afflictions. They have abandoned 
their afflictions through the wisdom that realises emptiness. The hearer and solitary realiser  also 
have the wisdom that realises emptiness. When th ey achieve liberation, they will have abandoned 
their afflictions from the root. But why is it that they cannot abandon the imprints of these 
afflictions, which the bodhisattva is able to do? This boils down to having bodhicitta. Bodhicitta 
is likened to the great sun. In the root text , “the great sun removes the misty ignorance.” 
3B2B 2A2A 3A2C  The potential [power]to accomplish all benefit and bliss 
1 Accomplishing all benefit 
2 Accomplishing all bliss 
3B2B 2A2A 3A2C 1 Accomplishing all benefit 
Bodhicitta has the power to accomplish all benefit as shown in last two lines of verse 32: “It is 
the quintessential butter from th e churning of the milk of Dh arma.” Bodhicitta is like 
quintessential butter -  the essence that we get fr om the churning of the milk of Dharma. When 
we listen to and reflect on the Dharma, the essenc e that we will extract from such listening and 
reflection would be bodhicitta. Bo dhicitta is said to be the esse nce of all the scriptures of the 
Buddha. Since bodhicitta is the essence of all the scriptures of  the Buddha,  bodhicitta can 
accomplish each and every single benefit. Since that  is the case, it is advisable to always reflect 
and meditate on bodhicitta all the time.  
Amitabha Buddhist Centre       Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds 
F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m              C h a p t e r  T h r e e  
 
 
151 3B2B 2A2A 3A2C 2 A ccomplishing all bliss 
Bodhicitta has the power to accomplish all bli ss and happiness and this is shown in verse 33: 
 
[3, 33] 
For all those guests travelling on the path of conditioned existence 
Who wish to experience the bounties of happiness, 
This will satisfy them with joy 
And actually place them in supreme bliss. 
 
Bodhisattvas work for all the six types of suffering  sentient beings circling in cyclic existence - 
from the peak of cyclic existence down to the Avici hell  -  who wi sh to experience both temporal 
and ultimate happiness,  and place them in supreme bliss instead of sorrowless nirvana thus 
satisfying them with joy. It is bodhicitta  that enables bodhisattvas to do this.  
 In the text it says, “For all those guests travelling  on the path of samsara”. The guests here refer to 
us, sentient beings in samsara. Why is the word “guests” used here? It describes the condition 
that we are in, always hurrying  from one place to the next, without an end in sight as to the 
n u m b e r  o f  p l a c e s  t h a t  o n e  h a s  t o  g o  t o .  D e s p i t e  h a v i n g  g o n e  t o  m a n y  p l a c e s ,  w e  h a v e  n e v e r  arrived anywhere. We are constantly on the move in the sense that we are constantly changing. 
We are always moving towards death in each and every single moment. We think that we will be 
staying for a while in this life but the fact is  that, in each and every single moment, we are 
moving closer and closer to death. When we reach death, we do not stop there. We have to take another rebirth again. When we die, we immedi ately have to go on to another rebirth. The 
number of rebirths we have taken is limi tless. That is the meaning of “guests.” 
3B2B 2A2A 3B Causing others to develop joy 
[3, 34] 
Today in the presence of all the Protectors 
I invite the world to be guests 
At (a festival of) temporary and ultimate delight. 
May gods, anti-gods and all be joyful. 
 
The words,  “I invite” indicate that we are inviti ng the guests. Who is this “I”? It is the person 
who has generated bodhicitta. When  do we invite the guest? We invite the guests now. From 
today, we invite the guests in the presence of and witnessed by all the buddhas and bodhisattvas . 
Who are the guests? It is the limitless number of se ntient beings. We invite all the guests so that 
we can offer them the state of en lightenment. Until they achieve the state of enlightenment, we 
offer  them the temporal benefit of higher rebi rths as humans and gods . By inviting all these 
guests, we give them whatever they need -  both temporal and ultimate gifts. Then we report our 
activities to all the gods and demigods (those beings from the white side who are supporting 
Amitabha Buddhist Centre       Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds 
F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m              C h a p t e r  T h r e e  
 
 
152 Dharma). When they hear of us doing this, all of them rejoice. We also ask them to protect us. 
This is the purpose of asking them to  protect those practising bodhicitta. 
 
We have completed  the third ch apter. The first three chapters cover the first two lines of the 
dedication prayer:  
May the precious bodhimind 
not yet born arise and grow. 
 
The commentary to the meaning of th ese two lines is now completed. 
 There is an advice from Gyaltsab Rinpoche at  the end of his commentary to this chapter:  
 
“First, one must reflect on the benefits of bodhicit ta. After reflecting on the benefits of bodhicitta, 
in order to eliminate the obstacles to the generati on of bodhicitta, one pu rifies or one confesses 
one’s negativities. In order to ga ther the favourable conditions fo r generating bodhicitta, one needs 
to accumulate merit. On this basis, one takes the bodhisattvas vows and one generates bodhicitta.”  
 
Rinpoche says that if we are able to accompli sh this, then we will have made our lives most 
meaningful. This is the best way. In conclusion , we should follow this advice: Listen, all the 
intelligent ones! The essence of al l the scriptures of the Buddha is  bodhicitta. Bodhicitta is the 
sole path travelled by bodhisattvas of the past. Pu t in effort in developing  the two bodhicittas; the 
first is aspirational bodhicitta, and then engaged bodhicitta.   The third line of the dedication prayer, “may that born have no decline”,  will be explained in the next three chapters. Chapter one explains the benefits of bodhicitta, chapter two confessing 
negativities and chapter three thoroughly embr acing bodhicitta – thes e are the methods for 
generating bodhicitta that has not yet been gene rated. Chapter four, conscientiousness,  chapter 
five, relying on vigilance, and chapter six, pati ence, present the methods to prevent bodhicitta 
from degenerating. “But increase forever more” refe rs to the methods to in crease bodhicitta that 
has been generated, presented in chapter se ven, joyous perseverance, chapter eight, 
concentration, and chapter nine, on wisdom. The la st chapter, chapter ten,  on dedication is a 
concluding prayer for dedications. 
3B2B 2A2B The chapter’s name 
The name of chapter three  is “Thoroughly embr acing bodhicitta” [or “Full Acceptance of the 
Awakening Mind”].

153 Lesson 19 – chapter 4, verse 1-10 
 
I would like to give you all an advice from a another text: 
 
 Just like an old person needs a walking stick to be able to walk properly, in order for us to 
understand the meaning of the teachi ngs, we need to rely on the wo rds. “Words” here  refers to the 
words of the texts, of the treatise s. It is important to memorize th eir contents, or the words of the 
text, in order to learn their mean ing. Otherwise we merely read the words, and our understanding 
and studies would never come to  a meaningful conclusion.  
 
What the author of this advice is trying to say is that in or der for one to really learn the 
teachings, first, one must have a really good gr asp of the words of the text that one would have 
already memorized. This advice was intended for those who were  studying in the monasteries. 
First, we must memorize the words of the text that we are studying. But just memorizing the 
words alone is not enough.  We may memorize the te xt and be able to recite it from memory but 
may not pay any attention to or reflect on the meaning of the words. This is exactly what 
happens when we perform pujas in the wrong way. If we sit at pujas, just reciting the prayers 
without reflecting on the meaning of the prayers,  we are no better than parrots. This is not the 
correct way to do pujas. If we teach a parrot to recite “Om mani padm e hum”, the parrot can 
recite “Om mani padme hum” 108 times. But that is about it.  When we do not reflect on the meaning of the words of the teachings that we have received, 
then we will not be able to cut any wrong or mi staken understanding. (Literally, we will not be 
able to cut any superimpositions). We really n eed to investigate those teachings in depth. In 
order to study the scriptures of the Buddha, first,  we must rely on the words. We must know the 
words of the text, but that alone is not sufficient.  We must also reflect on the meaning of those 
words. 
 This way of studying is not done here due to lack  of time. In the monasteries, they memorize all 
the root texts that they are studying and then read the commentaries. Here we do not have the 
time to memorize the words of the text. But when  different verses and stanzas are explained, at 
the very least, we should see whether we are ab le to understand the meaning of each of those 
stanzas. We have to check to see whether we are able to do that.  
The Fourth Chapter: Teaching Conscientiousness

bodhicitta and [its associated] conduct  
2 The way to train in ethics: A specific explanation given with regards to mindfulness and

wealth, and the roots of virtue for the welfare of others [Chapter Ten] 
 
The outline: “2B The way to train in the conduct of the perfections” has four major sub-headings 
that  run into the later chapters . This chapter only covers the fi rst point “The way to cultivate 
conscientiousness: The branch that prevents the deterioration of bodhicitta and [its associated] 
conduct”. The second sub-heading is  covered in chapter five, and so on.  
3B2B 2B1  The way to cultivate conscientiousness: The branch that prevents the 
deterioration of bodhicitta and [its associated] conduct 
A Explaining the chapter’s material 
B The chapter’s name 
3B2B 2B1A Explaining the chapter’s material 
1 A brief presentation of the way to cultivate conscientiousness 
2 An extensive explanation 
3 Synopsis 
3B2B 2B1A 1 A brief presentation of the way to cultivate conscientiousness 
[4,1] 
Having firmly seized the Aw akening Mind in this way, 
A Conqueror’s son must never waver; 
Always should he exert himself 
To never stray from his practice. 
 
Conscientiousness is the opposite of non-conscien tiousness. Non-conscientiousness is one of the 
twenty secondary afflictions and is a negative emotio n. It is a mind that does not guard or protect 
itself against the afflictions and the faults that arise from such  afflic tions. It is the mind that does 
whatever it wants without considering the co nsequences. That is non-conscientiousness. 
The function of non-conscientiousne ss is to increase negativities an d to weaken positive actions.  
 Conscientiousness is a mental factor, which is a mi nd that is not under the influence of negative 
emotions or afflictions. While it abides in joyous  effort or joyous persev erance, it accomplishes 
virtue. It is the mind that protec ts from contaminated phenomena. 
 The opposite of conscientiousness is non-consci entiousness.  Non-conscientiousness is a mind 
that does not protect from afflictions and the faults of afflictions. It is basically a mind that gives 
in to afflictions. Conscientiousness is the basis fo r the excellent collection of all the good things 
Amitabha Buddhist Centre       Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds 
F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m               C h a p t e r  F o u r  
 
 
155 of both samsara and nirvana. This is a brief explanation of conscientiousness. 
 
Verse 1 is a brief presentation of the way to cu ltivate conscientiousness. The essence is that 
having firmly seized both aspirational and en gaged bodhicitta - “having firmly seized the 
Awakening mind  in this way” - as explained in the previous chap ters, bodhisattvas should never 
stray from the practice of avoiding the 18 root downfalls and the 46 faults. Bodhisattvas should 
apply themselves to avoid committing any of these do wnfalls or faults; they should rely on joyous 
perseverance to do so without coming under the influence of laziness or procrastination.  After 
having firmly seized and thoroughly embraced bodhicitta, they  should rely on conscientiousness to keep the precepts.  “Firmly seized” refers to the time of taking the vows, when one has promised that one will never 
give up bodhicitta and one will never degenerate the practice even at the cost of one’s life. In the 
previous chapter, we looked at how the bodh isattva vows are taken. At that time, one has 
promised never to give up the practices, even at  the cost of one’s life. In that sense, one has 
thoroughly embraced and firmly seized bodhici tta in this way. After having taken the vows, 
bodhisattvas should always work at  keeping thei r vows and ensure that they do not degenerate.  
3B2B 2B1A 2 An extensive explanation 
A Cultivating conscientiousness with regards to bodhicitta 
B Cultivating conscientiousness with regards to the training 
3B2B 2B1A 2A Cultivating conscientiousness with regards to bodhicitta 
1 The reasons it is inappropriate to discard bodhicitta 
2 The disadvantages of discarding it 
3B2B 2B1A 2A1 The reasons why it is inappropriate to discard bodhicitta 
[4,2] 
In the case of reckless actions 
Or of deeds not well considered, 
Although a promise may have been made 
It is fit to reconsider whethe r I should do them or not. 
 
[4,3] 
But how can I ever withdraw 
From what has been examined by the great wisdom 
Of the Buddhas and their Sons, 
And even many times by me myself? 
 
“Reckless actions” refers to whatever actions we do: before we start any action, we do not 
consider the pros and cons of the action we inte nd to take. We do not think about or analyse the 
situation at all before we act. Even when we do  think about it, we do not thoroughly analyse the 
Amitabha Buddhist Centre       Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds 
F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m               C h a p t e r  F o u r  
 
 
156 situation before we decide to go ahead with a cert ain action. We then make a mental  promise, ‘I 
will complete this action.’  Sometimes, we br eak our promises when we do not complete our 
actions. In an ordinary situation,  this may still be all right.  
 But if we are talking about bodhicitta, it is no t appropriate and is not all right. In terms of 
ordinary actions, it may be all right to break or go against our promises.  But this is not the case 
with regards to bodhicitta. We should never give up bodhicitta because the benefits of bodhicitta 
have already been examined by those who po ssess great wisdom,  by all the buddhas and 
bodhisattvas, who  have seen all the wonder ful benefits of bodhicitta. The buddhas and 
bodhisattvas, who do not have even the slight est of faults and who possess great wisdom – 
referring to the great correct wisdom - have exam ined the benefits of bodhicitta in detail.  
 The last line of verse 3 says, “a nd even many times by me myself ”. We have also examined the 
benefits of bodhicitta many times. We should re member the very beginning of the text when we 
looked at many different benefits of bodhic itta. We have thought about bodhicitta, have 
reflected on and have seen its benefits.  Having  seen those benefits, we made the promise and 
took up the bodhisattva vows. If, after this whole pr ocess, we decide not to follow or  to give up 
our training and our bodhicitta, this is inapprop riate and incorrect. In fa ct, we should tighten 
and discipline the mind and focus on what we should  do in our training.   Conscientiousness is the mind that focuses on vi rtue after having seen both the faults and the 
advantages of certain actions. Conscientiousness fo cuses the mind on a virtuous course of action.  
 There are, therefore,  two reason s why it is inappropriate to give  up bodhicitta. The two reasons 
are: first, bodhicitta and its benefits have b een thoroughly examined by all the buddhas and 
bodhisattvas, who  have seen it to be a wonder ful thing; and second, we took the vows on the 
basis of clearly understanding the benefits of bodhicitta, we took the bodhisattva vows on the 
basis of having this clear understanding, therefore, it is inappropriate for us  to give up bodhicitta 
and our training now.   Because of these two reasons, we should rely on conscientiousness to make sure that our 
bodhicitta does not deteriorate or degenerate. If we do not have conscientiousness but, instead, 
have the opposite of conscientiousness,  which is non-conscientiousness, then the mind will be 
stained by the faults of the different transgre ssions of the bodhisattva vows. When we have 
conscientiousness, we will be prot ected against such  infractions.  
 Q. What is the difference between di scrimination and conscientiousness? 
 Discrimination is a mental factor that en ables the mind to apprehend an object.  
 
Amitabha Buddhist Centre       Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds 
F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m               C h a p t e r  F o u r  
 
 
157 Q. Between discrimination and conscientiousness, which is the mental factor that enables us to 
know what is virtue and what is non–virtue ?  
 
It is the mental factor of disc rimination that discriminates betw een virtue and non-virtue.  After 
having discriminated between what is virtue and  non-virtue, then conscientiousness focuses the 
mind on virtue and protects the mind from non-virtue.   The difference between verses 2 and  3: verse 2 re fers to actions other then giving up bodhicitta, 
such as ordinary worldly activities. We often do  n o t  c o n s i d e r  t h e  p r o s  a n d  c o n s  o f  a n  a c t i o n  
before we do it.   Even if we do think about the pros and cons, we may not analyse the situation 
thoroughly. In the case of ordi nary actions, after thinking ab out them thoroughly and then 
making the promise that, “I’m going to do this,” even if we do not follow through with or forget 
our promise, it may  still be  all right to brea k the promise. But this  is not the case with  
bodhicitta.   There are three faults or disadvan tages of giving up bodhicitta: 
3B2B 2B1A 2A2 The  disadvantages of discarding [bodhicitta] 
A The disadvantage of going to the lower realms 
B One ceases to work for the sake of others  
C Attainment of the grounds is postponed ∗    
3B2B 2B1A 2A2A The disadvantage of going to the lower realms 
1 The reasons one migrates to the lower realms 
2 Stating the proof for that 
3 Abandoning contradictions 
3B2B 2B1A 2A2A 1 The reasons one migrates to the lower realms 
[4,4] 
If having made such a promise 
I do not put it into action, 
Then by deceiving every living being 
What kind of rebirth shall I take? 
 
Why will we go to the lower realms if we break our promise by giving up bodhicitta? What are the promises we have made? In the presence of all sentient beings, we have invited them as guests 
and promised to liberate them from the suffering s of both samsara and nirvana. We also made 
the promise to bring all sentient beings to the st ate of full enlightenment. Having made such big 
promises, when it comes to the practice, if we do not  strive to live up to our promises and put 
them into action, then, we will  have deceived a ll the buddhas and all the sentient beings. We go 
to the lower realms because of committing this very  heavy negative action of deceiving them all. 
It is important to reflect on this particular faul t and rely on conscientiousness to protect and stop 
Amitabha Buddhist Centre       Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds 
F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m               C h a p t e r  F o u r  
 
 
158 the mind from committing  this fault of giving up bodhicitta. 
3B2B 2B1A 2A2A 2 Stating the proof for that 
 [4,5] 
If it has been taught (by the Buddha) 
That he who does not give away 
The smallest thing he once intended to give 
Will take rebirth as a hungry ghost;  
 
[4, 6 ] 
Then if I should deceive all beings 
After having sincerely invited them 
To the unsurpassable bliss, 
Shall I take a happy rebirth? 
 
The source for this proof is in the sutra titled The Close Placement of Mindfulness  by Buddha 
himself. It is taught,  in this  s u t r a ,  t h a t  w h e n  w e  d o  n o t  g i ve away something that we have 
thought of giving away (ie we al ready had  the intention of giving ), then we would  create the 
cause to be reborn as hungry ghosts. When we do not give away something that we have promised to give away, then that creates the cause for us to be reborn in the hells. If we were to 
make the promise of benefiting and liberating all sentient beings and yet do nothing about it or 
we  go against and   break that promise,  would we ever get a good rebirth?  If we have promised to accomplish the welfare and happiness of all se ntient beings, then, if we don’t do anything 
about it, go against the promise and give up the inte ntion to do so, we definitely go to the hells.  
3B2B 2B1A 2A2A 3 Abandoning contradictions 
[4, 7 ] 
Only the Omniscient can discern 
The manner of the action of those 
Who give up the Awaken ing Mind but are freed; 
It is beyond the scope of (ordinary) thought 
 
It has earlier been mentioned that,  if those who took the bodhisattva vows and made  the  
promise to benefit all sentient beings were to  break the vows and give up bodhicitta, they would 
definitely go to the hells. Having said that, there seems to be a contradiction in this  verse. Why? 
This is because there is an account of Shariputra  becoming an arhat  despite his having given up 
bodhicitta.   In one of his past lives, he took rebirth as a king named  Daiyu. In that rebirth, he developed 
bodhicitta, offered reverential service to 10,000 buddhas and worked for the benefit of sentient 
beings. One day, he met an emanation of mara, wh o appeared in the aspect of a  Brahmin. This 
Amitabha Buddhist Centre       Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds 
F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m               C h a p t e r  F o u r  
 
 
159 mara asked Shariputra for his right hand, which Sh ariputra, being a bodhisattva, duly cut off and 
gave  to the mara. As Shariputra had  cut off his right hand, he had to give his hand to the mara 
using his remaining left hand. The mara was disple ased and said “How can you do this in such a 
disrespectful way,  by giving me something with your left hand?” This mara took Shariputra’s 
right hand and threw it away. Shariputra became very discouraged after this incident and thought 
that there was no way that he could make sentient beings happy. So he gave up bodhicitta, fell to the lesser Hinayana path and achieved liberation in stead. He did not go to the lower realms but 
achieved liberation instead.   Why did Shariputra not go to the lower realms? The answer is given in the last line of verse 7: “it 
is beyond the scope of (ordinary)  thought”. This is because the subtle details of karma are the 
sole objects of knowledge of the buddhas alone an d are beyond the understanding of us ordinary 
beings. One commentary states  exactly the same po int but  goes a bit further: It is beyond the 
scope of ordinary thought, so do  not bother to even try to thin k why and how this can happen. If 
we try to figure this out, we will get a headac he and go crazy, as this is something only the 
buddhas can understand! When we look at all ph enomena in existence or objects of knowledge, 
they can be categorized into three: manifest phenomena, slightly obscured phenomena, and 
extremely obscured phenomena.   Extremely obscured phenomena include these very su btle details of karma. We can only hope to 
understand this class of extrem ely obscured phenomena by depend ing on the scriptural authority 
of the buddhas. It is beyond our direct experience  and there is no way that we can prove it with 
any logic and reasoning.  To reiterate: manifest phenomena refers to the class of phenomena which we can directly 
experience. We can understand these objects without relying on any reasons since we can 
experience them directly. 
2. Slightly obscured, or slightly hidden phenom ena refers to those things that we can only 
understand by initially depending on logic and reasoning, or inference. 
3. Extremely obscured or very hidden phenomen a refers to those things that we can only 
understand, believe or have conviction in by depending  on the scriptures of the Buddha.

1 As the deterioration of bodhicitta involves a seri ous [lit. heavy] downfall, the welfare of others 
deteriorates 2 It is equivalent to obstructing the virtue of another bodhisattva [and thus] one migrates to the 
lower realms ∗ 
3 The reasons for that 
3B2B 2B1A 2A2B  1 As the deterioration of bodhicitta involves a serious [lit. heavy] downfall, 
the welfare of others deteriorates 
[4,8] 
Amitabha Buddhist Centre       Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds 
F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m               C h a p t e r  F o u r  
 
 
160 This, for a Bodhisattva, 
Is the heaviest of downfalls, 
For should it ever happen, 
The welfare of all will be weakened 
 
Giving up bodhicitta is the heaviest of the many different root downfalls of the bodhisattva vows.  
If we give up bodhicitta, then the welfare of ot hers will deteriorate as well. Why? Bodhicitta, the 
mind of the altruistic intention, is the basis for helping others. Therefore, if we give up 
bodhicitta, the welfare of ot hers will deteriorate.  
 Imagine a bodhisattva who possesses both pratim oksha vow and bodhisattva vows. When  that 
bodhisattva gives up bodhicitta, th at negative action is much heavier than committing a defeat of 
the pratimoksha vow. Commi tting a defeat of pratimoksha vows is  a very serious negative action. 
But the act of giving up bodhici tta is a much heavier negative action.  When   we give up 
bodhicitta, it  stops the be nefit of others and the welfare of others deteriorates. 
3B2B 2B1A 2A2B 2 It is equivalent to obstructing the virtue of another bodhisattva [and thus] 
one migrates to the lower realms 
This is equivalent to stopping or degenera ting one’s work for the benefit of others. 
 
[4,9] 
And should others for even a single moment 
Hinder or obstruct th eir wholesome (deeds) 
By weakening the welfare of all 
There will be no end to their rebirth in lower states. 
 
If someone were to obstruct or create obstacles to another bodhisattva’s practice of virtue, that 
obstruction, by hindering or creating problems for that bodhisattva’s virtuous activities,  would weaken that bodhisattva’s ability to benefit sentie nt beings.  By doing this, one creates the cause 
to take many rebirths in the lower realms.   Bodhisattvas are always continuously working for the benefit of others. When we obstruct their 
activities, we are creating obstacles to the welfar e and happiness of all sentient beings. When that 
happens, we accumulate negativities. Because of those negativities, we will take rebirth in the lower realms. 
3B2B 2B1A 2A2B 3 The reasons for that 
Since we do not know who is and wh o is not a bodhisattva, it  is advisable to be extremely careful 
not to stop the virtuous activities of others. If  the person happens to be a bodhisattva, then we 
will be in trouble. What is the reason  for that? This is shown in verse 10: 
 
Amitabha Buddhist Centre       Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds 
F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m               C h a p t e r  F o u r  
 
 
161  
[4,10] 
For if my being is impaired 
By destroying the joy of even one sentient being, 
Then what need is there to mention 
Destroying the joy of sentient beings, vast as space? 
 
If we were to destroy the happiness of just one sentient being, we would  get into trouble and 
suffer. There is no need then to talk about the suffering that we will have to endure if we destroy the happiness of all sentient beings as vast as space.   In some other commentaries, the reasons why we go  to the lower realms when  we obstruct the 
virtue of another bodhisattva are explained in tw o ways: reasoning employing scriptural authority  
reasoning employing  logic  Verse 10 establishes  the reason using  logic. Dest roying the happiness of just one sentient being 
will cause us not to be reborn in the higher real ms. It goes without saying  then that there will be 
much more suffering if we destroy the happiness of all sentient beings. Why is it such a negative 
action to obstruct the activities of a bodhis attva? Because, by causing obstacles to the 
bodhisattva’s practice of virtue, we are actually  causing obstacles to th e cause of a buddha; the 
cause of enlightenment. By obstructing the works of a bodhisattva, we are creating obstacles to 
the cause of happiness of all sentient beings, the enlightenment of all sentient beings.   
  
Amitabha Buddhist Centre       Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds 
F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m               C h a p t e r  F o u r  
 
 
162 Lesson 20 – chapter 4, verse 10-17 
 
Buddha said in the King of Concentrations Sutra :  
 
I have explained this very good teaching.  
Yet if you, having heard it, do not practise correctly,  
Then just like a sick person hold ing on to a bag of medicine,  
Your illness cannot be cured.  
 
This verse from the sutra can be applied to us be cause we listen to and study the teachings but we 
find it difficult to reflect on their meaning and to make them useful; we are unable to put them 
into practice. That is why we do not find ou r minds improving or ourselves becoming more 
good-hearted. We may listen to many teaching s but we do not necessarily reflect on their 
meaning. Because of that, we do not see any improvement in ourselves.  
 Instead, we experience mental unhappiness and su ffering. In fact, sometimes, it seems that we 
are experiencing even more suffering than before . This is the fault of not reflecting on the 
meaning of the teachings that we have heard. We  are just like the patient who carries a bag of 
medicine around without taking any. If we do no t take the medicine, there is no way that we can 
recover from our sicknesses. We need to reflect on the meaning of the te achings that we have 
heard in order to remove our problems and the extensive suffering that we have endured for a very long time.   When we do not engage in the activities of list ening, reflecting and familiarising our minds with 
those teachings over a long period of time, we are not going to be able to recover or free ourselves from our problems because our sufferings have been there for very long time.  We need to understand that the patient carrying the ba g of medicine, mentioned by the Buddha in this 
sutra, is actually referring to us. We need to put down the bag of medicine that we have been 
carrying on our backs, open the ba g and start taking the medicine. It  is not enough to just hear 
the teachings. We must start reflecting on them.  
We are now studying the text, Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds. It contains many inconceivable 
precepts, advice and teachings. What we are doing is  listening to and learning  what is in this text. 
It may be difficult to put the teachings into practi se immediately but, at the very least, we should 
reflect on the meaning of the word s that are found in the text; we should not just leave it at the 
level of listening or looking at the words. We have  to try to reflect on the words themselves, what 
is in the text.   Before class, we do certain prayers such as ma king the mandala offering. That is the time we 
should put into practise the many different ways of making offerings and the visualisations that 
Amitabha Buddhist Centre       Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds 
F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m               C h a p t e r  F o u r  
 
 
163 we have learnt. When we are offering the mandal a, we should try to visualise those extensive 
offerings explained in the text. We visualise and then offer them to all the buddhas and 
bodhisattvas. When we are able to do that, we will accumulate an inconceivable amount of merit 
within a short period of time.  We need to put into practice what we have lear nt. After that, we recite the verse of going for 
refuge and generating bodhicitta. We have ta lked about the meaning of refuge and how we 
should go for refuge. We have also talked about the way we should develop the altruistic 
intention of bodhicitta. At the very least then, wh ile reciting that verse, we should be able to 
bring forth some sort of feeling for the verse by reflecting on what we have learnt and try to 
generate the appropriate attitudes.  It is important to reflect, as much as we can, to the best of our abilities, on what we have learnt and the meaning of whatever prayers we may be reci ting. Why do we remain as we are; we do not 
change and improve? It boils down to the fact th at we did not reflect on what we have heard.  
 All of us have to try our very be st to reflect on the meaning of th e words of the teachings that we 
have heard and try to improve our own minds be cause improving the state of our minds is an 
individual responsibility. Kyabje Zopa Rinpoche’s holy wish for the centre is to produce good-hearted human beings. Rinpoche’s vision for setting  up the centre is not just to produce people 
who have some intellectual understanding of the teachings. His purpose of setting up the centre 
is to provide an opportunity to develop good-hea rted people and good human beings. That is his 
real wish. We should all try our very best to make this happen. It is not easy . It is difficult but we 
just have to try our best.  
3B2B 2B1A 2A2 The  disadvantages of discarding [bodhicitta] 
A The disadvantage of going to the lower realms 
B One ceases to work for the sake of others  
C Attainment of the grounds is postponed ∗    
3B2B 2B1A 2A2B  Attainment of  the grounds is postponed    
[4,11] 
Thus those who have the force of an Awakening Mind 
As well as the force of falling (from it) 
Stay revolving within cyclic existence 
And for a long time are hindered fr om reaching the Bodhisattva levels. 
 
We have already seen some of the faults of giving  up bodhicitta: one will go to the lower realms 
and be reborn in the hells and one’s work for othe rs will degenerate. There are those who say, ‘If 
I degenerate or break my bodhisattva vows, it is OK as I can confess it and retake the vows again.’ 
It is true that we can retake the vows and genera te bodhicitta again but attaining the bodhisattva 
Amitabha Buddhist Centre       Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds 
F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m               C h a p t e r  F o u r  
 
 
164 grounds will be postponed. This is because we crea te the cause to go to the lower realms when we 
give up bodhicitta. When we generate bodhicitta  again, we create the cause to gain a good 
rebirth. So we are still stuck in sa msara, going back to square one.  
 When we give up bodhicitta, the attainment of the first ground is postponed. When attainment 
of the first ground is postponed, then obviously the attainment of enlightenment is postponed.  
Eg. you  try to move an object closer to you bu t at the same time, there is someone trying to 
move that same object closer to himself. So the object will move to and fro and after an hour, the 
object basically remains in the same position.    In another commentary it is mentioned that when  we commit a root downfall of the bodhisattva 
vows we can purify it by confessing the negativi ty, retaking the vows and generating bodhicitta 
again. Because of that purification practice, one may not be born in the lower realms but, 
nevertheless, the attainment of th e bodhisattvas ground is postpo ned. Why? This is because the 
occurrence of the root downfall will act as an obstacle for developing new qualities. 
 Why is it that, despite purifying the negativities that come with committing the root downfall, it 
becomes difficult to acquire new qualities? This is something for you to think about:  if we purify 
the negativities of having committed the root downfall through a complete purification by 
applying the four opponent powers, how is it that one’s attainment of new qualities will be 
postponed?  We have been looking at the practices of cultivat ing conscientiousness with regards to bodhicitta. 
Once we have developed bodhicitta, we take the vows. We have to try not to let the vows 
degenerate. In order to do this, we need to rely on conscientiousness.   
S o  f a r ,  w e  h a v e  l o o k e d  a t  t h e  f a u l t s  o r  d i s a d v antages of giving up bo dhicitta. There are three 
main faults mentioned in the text. If we give up bodhicitta: we create the cause to go to the lower 
realms, our work for others degenerates; and our attainment of the bodhisattva grounds is 
postponed. The point is to focus the mind to be conscientious about keeping the vows, not losing or letting them degenerate and not adopti ng a careless attitude towards them. We should 
reflect on these different faults. We should remind ourselves that these are the faults if we let our 
bodhicitta degenerate or lose ou r vows. By remembering these faults, we should focus our minds, 
apply joyous perseverance and make the effort to  keep the vows. What we have been discussing 
so far are the ways to stop bodhicitta from degenerating.  How do we stop bodhicitta from degenerating? Fi rst, we reflect on the faults of giving up 
bodhicitta. By reflecting on the faults, we focus our minds and make the decision that “I will not 
let my bodhicitta degenerate.”

3 Being conscientious about abandoning afflictions

lower realms

3B2B 2B1A 2B1A  If negativities and downfa lls are not abandoned, one must continue [to 
take rebirth] in the lower realms 
[4,12] 
Therefore just as I have promised 
Shall I respectfully accord my actions. 
If from now on I make no effort 
I shall descend from lower to lower states. 
 
B y  r e f l e c t i n g  o n  t h e  f a u l t s  o f  g i v i n g  u p  b o dhicitta, we will engage in the training of 
conscientiousness, in the same way we have promis ed to follow the trainings of the bodhisattvas 
during our taking of the bodhisattva vows. From th en on, if we do not put in any effort, because 
of the fault of committing a root downfall, we wi ll descend to lower and lower states and take 
rebirth in the lower realms.  Now we are talking about cultivating conscientiousn ess with regards to the training so that our 
vows will not be stained and we will not commit a downfall. If we were to commit a downfall, we 
should remember that we would have to take re birth in the lower realms. It says in verse 12, 
“Therefore just as I have promised, I shall re spectfully accord my actions.” So one acts 
respectfully, with conscientiousness, with regards to the training.  We took the vows respectfully 
– no one forced us to do it. In the same way,  keeping the vows and engaging in the trainings 
should be done with a respectful attitude.  
3B2B 2B1A 2B1B  The Buddhas and their children act with equanimity   
[4,13] 
Although for the benefit of every creature 
Countless Buddhas have passed by, 
Yet I was not an object of their care 
Because of my own mistakes. 
  
Amitabha Buddhist Centre       Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds 
F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m               C h a p t e r  F o u r  
 
 
166 [4,14] 
And if I continue to act like this, 
Again and again shall I undergo 
(Suffering) in unhappy realms, sickness, bondage, 
Laceration and the shedding of blood. 
 
We do not put effort in protecting ourselves fr om the root downfalls of the bodhisattva vows and 
in creating virtue, thinking, ‘It is OK if I canno t engage in virtue and protect myself from this 
root downfall, because my gurus and the buddhas and bodhisattvas will help me. My gurus and the buddhas and bodhisattvas will pluck me out of the lower realms, send me off to a good 
rebirth and place me on the path.’  Countless buddhas have come and gone for the benefit of all sentient beings. Somehow, we did 
not come under their care. Although countless bu ddhas have passed, “I was not an object of 
their care.” Why?  As mentioned in the root text - “Because of my own mistakes” –this is because 
of the fault of having accumulated negativities. Th is verse is not saying that the buddhas have no 
power. The buddhas have power, but there must also be conditions from our side. Though the 
buddhas have power, due to our own faults, we did not come under their care.  
In the eighth chapter of his Ornament for Clear Realisations (Abhisamayalamkara) , Maitreya Buddha 
said that just as dead seeds will not grow even if all the conditions,  such as rainfall, fertiliser, soil, 
warmth and so forth are present, similarly,  beca use of our own faults and mistakes, we have not 
come under the care of the buddhas. The buddhas  have complete power but, in order for that 
p o w e r  t o  b e  e f f e c t i v e ,  w e  m u s t  b e  r e a d y  f r o m  our own sides. Because of our own faults, this 
power does not have any effect. In this case, th erefore, it is not the fault of the buddhas.  
 The unsuitable seed mentioned above is an analog y. We should apply that  analogy to what we 
are studying here; if we are not conscientious about our vows, do not guard them, break them or commit a root downfall, then it is our own fault. Because of creating such faults and negativities, 
the buddhas are unable to help and protect us.   If we talk about the seed from the perspective of our buddha nature, of course, all sentient beings 
have buddha nature. When we talk about the dege neration of the seed, it refers to our buddha 
nature being bound or chained by our negativities.  We have to remove these faults ourselves.  
 Sometimes, we go to the other extreme: “If I possess all the potential and power to become a 
buddha, then I do not need the buddhas. What do  I need the buddhas for?” If we are thinking 
like that, we are implying that our buddha nature is solid and inherently existent because it does 
not need to rely on any other factors.   
Amitabha Buddhist Centre       Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds 
F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m               C h a p t e r  F o u r  
 
 
167 The hearers and the solitary realisers arise from the buddhas and th e buddhas arise from 
bodhicitta. Whatever goals we may have, be it to ac hieve the level of a hearer, solitary realiser or 
buddha, we all need to rely on the teaching s of the Buddha. We ac hieve enlightenment by 
depending on the teachings or scriptures of the Buddha. We will not be able to achieve 
enlightenment without depending on the advice and the teachings of th e Buddha. We need all 
these conditions before we can achieve enli ghtenment. We will not be able to achieve 
enlightenment on our own, without de pending on these other factors.  
 Using again the analogy of the seed, even if the seed possessed the potential to transform into a 
plant, the seed alone would not be able to do this without depending on other conditions such 
as fertilisers, warmth, water and so forth. In the same way, although we may have the buddha 
nature or the potential to become a buddha,  that alone will not help us to achieve 
enlightenment.  The main advice here is that we need to strive conscientiously not to be stained by faults in the first place. When we are stained by the faults, then the buddhas wi ll not be able to protect us. 
Some people might think, “Never mind. Even if I am not protecting my vows or am careless now, 
I  w i l l  n o t  b e  c a r e l e s s  t h e  n e x t  t i m e .  I t  i s  O K  i f  I  c r e a t e  n e g a t i v i t i e s  n o w .  E v e n  i f  I  a m  n o t  protected now, I will be protected in the future.” Thinking in such a way is a mistake. As long we do not stop creating negativities, adopting a careless and reckless attitude, doing whatever we want, we will be stained by downfalls and not become objects of protection by the buddhas. In fact, the day when we will receive such protection  will be postponed.  Because of creating these 
negativities again and again, we will be reborn  and undergo suffering in the lower realms. While 
there, we will have to experience all the problems  - sicknesses, bondage, being cut and beaten up 
and tortured.   
The buddhas and bodhisattvas always act with equa nimity. It is not that they do not protect us 
but if we commit faults, then they cannot help us . The point is to refrain from being stained by 
the faults by relying on conscientiousness.

1 If bodhicitta deteriorates, it becomes difficult to obtain leisures and endowments that possess 
the four wheels - conditions  [that facilitate practice] 
2 Even though they have been obtained, one should make effort because they quickly perish 
3B2B 2B1A 2B1C 1 If bodhicitta deteriorates, it  becomes difficult to obtain a human life of 
leisures and endowments that possess the four  wheels- conditions [tha t facilitate practice] 
[4,15] 
If the arising of a Tathagata, 
Faith, the attainment of a human body 
And my being fit to cultivate virtue are scarce, 
When will they be won again? 
Amitabha Buddhist Centre       Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds 
F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m               C h a p t e r  F o u r  
 
 
168  
Verse 15 talks about the ten opportunities posse ssed by a human life of leisure and endowments: 
the five endowments that relate to others and  the five endowments that  relate to ourselves. 
 “The arising of a Tathagata” or the coming of the Buddha to any world is very rare. The other 
four opportunities related to others are also im plied:  (1) the Buddha ta ught the Dharma, (2) the 
Dharma abides, (3) there are people engaging in the teaching, practice and study of the Dharma 
and (4) there are people who support us in our Dharma practice.  The “attainment of a human body” refers to the fi ve opportunities related to oneself which are – 
(1) one is a human being, (2) one is born in a ce ntral place, (3) one is born with complete sense 
faculties, (4) one has not committed any of the five heinous crimes or the five uninterrupted karmas and (5) one has faith in the teachings.  The eight leisures are implied, thus completing th e 18 characteristics of a human life of leisure 
and opportunity. Having obtained this kind of rebirt h, if we do not use it to cultivate virtue now, 
when will we get such a rebirth again in the futu re? If the attainment of a human life of leisure 
and opportunity is so difficult, then it is even more difficult, on the basis of attaining such a 
human life, to be able to generate bodhicitta an d to engage in the trainings. When will this 
chance of generating bodhicitta and engagi ng in the trainings, ever happen again? 
 “The leisures and endowments that  possess the four wheels - conditio ns [that facilitate practice]” 
The four wheels or conditions referred to here are:  
1. to be born in a conducive environment with  harmonious friends who assist us in the 
practice of virtue;  
2. t o  b e  a b l e  t o  r e l y  o n  h o l y  b e i n g s  w i t h  s p e c i f i c  r e f e r e n c e  t o  t h e  f a c t   t h a t  w e  h a v e  t h e  
opportunity to meet and rely on Mahayana gurus;  
3. as a result of virtuous prayers made in the pa st, to engage in virtue enthusiastically with 
one’s body, speech and mind ; 
4. to have good and favourable conditions for th e practice of the Mahayana teachings. This 
comes about as the result of having accu mulated or performed virtue in the past. 
 These four wheels are the four Mahayana sphere s mentioned in the dedication prayer of the 
Guru Puja practice: 
By the force of this merit in all my lives 
May I never be parted from the Mahayana’s four spheres 
And may I reach the end of my journey along the paths of  
Renunciation, bodhicitta, the pure view, and the two stages 
 
(From the FPMT Prayer Book , page 205,  LC 117.) 
Amitabha Buddhist Centre       Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds 
F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m               C h a p t e r  F o u r  
 
 
169 Thus it is very important for us to recognise that the eight leisur es and ten opportunities are very 
difficult to find and we need to check whether we posses all these 18 char acteristics. If we do 
have most of them, we should practise the Dharma as what we have obtained is very rare indeed. 
But if we do not make use of our present existence to the fullest for practising Dharma, it will be 
extremely difficult to gain such a beneficially endowed form again. 
3B2B 2B1A 2B1C 2 Even though they have been obtained, one should make effort because 
they quickly perish 
Even if we have already obtained this human life of leisure and opportunity, we should still make 
an effort as it will perish very quickly. 
[4,16] 
Although today I am healthy, 
Well-nourished and unafflicted, 
Life is momentary and deceptive: 
The body is like an object on loan for but a minute. 
 
At the present moment, we may be healthy, with no major sicknesses, well- clothed and well fed 
and have no enemies who create problems for us  (“unafflicited” means unharmed by enemies). 
Although this may be our present situation,  our life spans are unstable, momentary and 
deceptive. What does “deceptive” refer to? “Deceptive” refers to the nature of our life spans. 
Although our life spans seem very stable, in real ity, they are not so. Ther e is a disparity between 
appearance and reality because our life spans are disintegrating in each and every single moment. 
They are being continuously exhausted. 
 Our bodies are like objects on loan for a very sh ort time. Our bodies do not belong to us. When 
the time comes, the owner, the Lo rd of Death, will take our bodies from us. We have to return 
and give up our bodies and die. We have now ob tained a human life of leisure and opportunity 
where there are no obstacles and all the favourab le conditions are gather ed together. At this 
time, our life spans appear to be stable. In real ity, however, our life spans and our bodies are 
disintegrating in each and every single moment. Because of that, we must make the effort from 
now on to abandon our negativities.

F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m               C h a p t e r  F o u r  
 
 
170 [4,17] 
And with behaviour such as this 
I shall not win a human body again, 
And if this human form is not attained 
There will be solely evil and no virtue. 
 
It is incorrect to think, “I will always get a good rebirth and when  I get such a good rebirth again 
in the future, then I will practise.” Why is it incorrect to think in such a way? Because if we 
continue our present behaviour of committing negati ve actions and not cultivating virtue, we will 
not get a human rebirth again. Once we are in  the lower realms, we will commit negativities 
continuously and have no chance to create virtue . That being the case, we will always remain in 
the lower realms.  We should apply this to ourselves - we may think,  “Never mind if I mess up this life. It’s OK. I 
will do better in the next life when I get another rebirth.” If we mess up this life, we will also 
mess up the next life. We will then go to the lowe r realms and once we are there, it will difficult 
to get out. We are all like this. We do not do anything when all the favourable conditions are 
present and we just spend our lives in an empty way.    It is clear that once we are in the lower realms, ther e is no opportunity to prac tise virtue. If that is 
the case, how will we get a good rebirth again? This  is advice for us, to motivate ourselves in our 
Dharma practice and to start the prac tice of abandoning negativities.  
 In this context, we are referring to being consci entious about the training. First, we should be 
conscientious about abandoning negativities. Havi ng obtained this human life of leisure and 
opportunity, we should be conscientious about abandoning negativities.  
 
If we do not reflect on what we have covered earlier, we will be come unconscientious, adopting a 
‘can’t-be-bothered’ attitude. With such an a ttitude, we will be stained by many faults, 
transgressions and negativities. Once that happens, we will go to the lower realms. We will have to experience unimaginable sufferings once we are there.  We can avoid this situation if we contemplate the points we have discussed so far. When we end 
up in the lower realms, it will be very difficult to get a good rebirth again because we will be committing negativities continuously and there wi ll be no chance for virtue. We do not even 
have to talk about the hell realms. Look at the animals around us. They are so foolish and completely blinded by ignorance. Even when we tr y to teach them to do so me virtue, they cannot 
do it. Therefore, since we have obtained this hu man life of leisure and opportunity, we should 
try as much as we can to abandon ne gativities and to cultivate virtue.

171  
Lesson 21 – chapter 4, verse 18-27 
 
The great Indian master, Chandragomin,  said that  if someone is very sick and is down with a 
serious disease, like leprosy, but does not take proper medicine continuously over a period of time – only doing so when he feels like it - then, that person will never recover from his illness. This is an analogy for the situat ion that we are in. We have been under the influence and control 
of the three mental poisons for a very long time. We have been under the control of ignorance.  
 In order to free ourselves, we have to familiarise ourselves with and meditate on the antidotes continuously for a very long time. If we only medi tate sometimes, we will never be able to free 
ourselves from those afflictions. When we talk abou t removing the afflictions, we need to train in 
the path that is complete. It does not mean doin g any virtue that we like and then hoping or 
expecting the afflictions to just weaken or disappe a r .  I t  d o e s  n o t  w o r k  l i k e  t h a t .   W e  h a v e  t o  
meditate on the complete path.   We do engage in virtuous practices, but some times we feel that, despite doing all sorts of 
practices, we are not getting anywhere. We ar e not improving. This is how we may feel 
sometimes. Actually, things are getting better but we should not expect to see instant results. 
Sometimes, when we engage in certain practices, we  expect to see results in  a day, a month, a year 
or even a couple of years. It does not work like that. We may not be able to see very tangible results for quite a while.   Our afflictions are like the very heavy sicknesses of a patient. We have been harbouring these 
afflictions, the three mental poisons, in our mi nds for a very long time.  In order to heal 
ourselves of these afflictions, we need to medita te and rely on the antidotes continuously for a 
long period of time. If we rely on the antidotes every now and then, as and when we feel like it, 
then we are not going to reap much benefit from them.  When it comes to Dharma practice or studies, we  should not be lazy. Sometimes we think, “I am 
getting old, I am not intelligent enough to unde rstand this, I do not have enough time” and so 
forth, and we put ourselves down. When we think like this, we are actually stopping ourselves from taking advantage of the opportunity for Dh arma studies and practice. Because of thinking 
in such a way, we do not study an d practise. Then we become lazy.  
 We should not stop ourselves from having a fair share of Dharma practice or study. All of us are different; some are predisposed towards ange r, others are predisposed towards mental 
distractions. Some people might think, “I am the angry sort and there is no hope for me. It is 
impossible for me to meditate on compassion. Forg et about it.”  When people think in such a 
way, they stop giving themselves  an opportunity to improve.  
Amitabha Buddhist Centre       Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds 
F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m               C h a p t e r  F o u r  
 
 
172 Some people might think, “My mind is so distracted . I have so many distractions, thinking of this 
and that. There is no way I can meditate. There is no way I can develop concentration.” When 
they think in such a way, they stop themselv es from being able to do anything about it. 
 The point here is not to create obstacles for ou r own Dharma practice. We should open the door 
to our own Dharma practice and study. We have already talked about a human life of leisure and 
opportunity. This is something on which we shou ld reflect. We have the ability to study and 
practise the teachings and all the g ood conditions are gathered together to enable us to do so. By 
reflecting in such a way, we should encourag e ourselves and persuade our mind to practise 
Dharma, to open the door to Dharma practice.

3B2B 2B1A 2B1D 2 If one does not make effort when when one has obtained a higher rebirth,

[4,18] 
If when I have the chance to live a wholesome life

Then what shall I be able to do 
When confused by the misery of the lower realms? 
 
We are fortunate now to have obtained this good rebirth. At such a time, if we do not practise 
some virtue, in the future, when we take rebirth in  the lower realms, as the result of the ripening 
of negativities, we will be tormented by various sufferings and we will be confused and ignorant as to what is to be abandoned and what is to be practised.  
 Now, when we have the opportunity, we should practise virtue. We need to remind ourselves t h a t ,  a t  t h i s  t i m e  w h e n  w e  h a v e  a  h u m a n  l i f e  o f  l e i s u r e  a n d  o p p o r t u n i t y ,  w e  s h o u l d  s t r i v e  t o

3B2B 2B1A 2B1D 3 It is extremely  difficult to be liberated from the lower realms [once one has

Amitabha Buddhist Centre       Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds 
F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m               C h a p t e r  F o u r  
 
 
173 [4,19] 
And if I commit no wholesome deeds (there), 
But readily amass much evil, 
Then for a hundred million aeons 
I shall not even hear the words “a happy life.” 
  
It will be difficult to free ourselves from the lowe r realms once we are there.  Why? The reason is 
given in verse 19. As we are unable to accumulate any virtue there, while at the same time readily 
amassing much negativity, for hundreds of mill i o n s  o f  e o n s ,  w e  w i l l  h a v e  t o  t a k e  r e b i r t h  
continuously in the lower realms. We will not be  able to obtain a happy rebirth. Putting aside 
getting a good rebirth, we will not even hear the words “good rebirth.”   If we accept past and future lives, that effects will follow after causes and that the results of our 
actions will follow us into our future lives, thinking about this verse will generate fear in our minds. The point though is not ju st to be frightened and then do nothing about our fears. This 
is not beneficial. Instead, when we are fright ened, we should think about obtaining a good 
rebirth and reflect on what are the causes that wo uld bring about such a good rebirth. The causes 
of a good rebirth are the practices of virtue. The co nclusion then is to practise as much virtue as 
we can and to abandon, as far as we able, even the slightest non-virtue.  
3B2B 2B1A 2B1E  The reason why it is difficu lt to obtain the leisures and endowments 
[4,20] 
For these very reasons, the Buddha has said 
That hard as it is for a turtle to insert its neck 
Into a yoke adrift upon the vast ocean, 
It is extremely hard to attain the human state 
 
“For these very reasons,” in the first line of vers e 20 refers to the reasons mentioned in the earlier 
verse – why it is difficult to get out of the lower realms once we are born there.   The analogy entails imagining the whole planet be coming an ocean and a buoy floating around 
on its surface, moved around by the wind. Beneat h the ocean, there is a blind turtle that comes 
to the surface of the ocean once every hundred year s to take a breath of air. What are the chances 
of this turtle poking its head th rough the centre of the buoy? It is said that it is even more 
difficult than this to attain a human life of le isure and opportunity.  This is establishing the 
difficulty of obtaining a human life of le isure and opportunity through an analogy. 
 
In the Lam Rim Chenmo , in the section on “A Human Life  of Leisure and Opportunity”, we 
talked about the establishing of a human life of  leisure and opportunity through causes, entity 
and analogy. Here it is done through analogy. Th is analogy helps us to understand the difficulty 
of obtaining a human life of leisure and opportun ity. We should reflect and check to see whether 
Amitabha Buddhist Centre       Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds 
F P M T  B a s i c  P r o g r a m               C h a p t e r  F o u r  
 
 
174 it is really difficult to obtain a human life of le isure and opportunity. In this analogy, the ocean is 
likened to cyclic existence, covering everything from the top, the peak of samsara down to the 
very bottom, the Avici hell. 
 The teachings of the Buddha are very rare. The Bu ddha’s teachings do not exist all the time. We 
can divide the existence of the world system into  different stages called the eon of darkness and 
the eon of illumination. It is said that the eon of illumination is very short.  
 The vast ocean is the realm of cyclic existence. Wh ere we take rebirth in cyclic existence is not up 
to us; we have no choice whatsoever. We are th rown from one rebirth to another according to 
our karma and afflictions. Think ab out this. The eon of darkness is said to last for a very long 
time and the eon of illumination, a very shor t time. The occurrence of the Buddha and his 
teachings are also very rare. When we look at our own lives, how much virtue is there in what we 
do? When we honestly look and compare the virtue  and non-virtue that we have accumulated, we 
have accumulated much more non-virt ue. If that is the case, obviousl y, it is going to be difficult 
to obtain another good rebirth. If this is so for oneself, then it must be so for others as well.  
 Some people might think that it is not difficult to get a good rebirth as there are so many human beings around. What we are discussing here is whether it is difficult to obtain a human life of leisure and opportunity. We can infer this from looking at our own lives. If you happen to be 
someone who is always engaging in virtue, then obtaining a human life of leisure and 
opportunity would not be difficult  for you. If we are under th e control of the three mental 
poisons constantly, then obtaining a human life of leisure and opportunity in the future would 
be difficult.  If we are unable to   practise virtue now and end up in the lower realms, as mentioned earlier, we will not get another good rebirth for hundreds of millions of eons. Once 
we find ourselves in the lower realms, it will be  almost impossible to get out. It will be almost 
impossible to get another human life of  leisure and opportunity again.   
 All the points that we have been talking so far falls under the outline of being conscientious to 
abandon negativities.

175 [4,21] 
If even by the evil of one instant 
An aeon may be spent in the deepest hell, 
Then because of the evil I have gathered since beginningless time, 
What need to mention my not going to a happy realm? 
 
The Buddha taught that even an instant of ange r towards a bodhisattva would cause one to take 
rebirth in hell for an eon. It goes without saying that we will have to spend a very long time in the lower realms due to the results of the immeas urable negativities that we have accumulated 
since time without beginning.  Reflecting on th is, we come to understanding why we need to 
cultivate virtue and to purify the negativities accumulated in the past by applying the four 
opponent powers.  
3B2B 2B1A 2B2B  The reasons why the karma [that leads one to take rebirth in] the lower 
realms is not exhausted by merely experiencing suffering in the lower realms one time 
[4,22] 
But having experienced merely  that (rebirth in hell) 
I shall still not be liberated; 
For while it is being experienced 
Other evil will be extensively produced. 
 
Even if we undergo the sufferings of the lower real ms and the suffering is exhausted, we will not 
be liberated from the lower realms . Why? This is because while we  are experiencing the sufferings 
of the lower realms, we accumulate a fresh lot of  negativities. Once we are in the lower realms, 
any virtue that we do will be very weak. At  the same time, negativities are accumulated 
continuously.   Therefore, it is important to strive to stop ours elves from going to the lower realms in the very 
first place. At the very least, after having obtain ed this human life of leisure and opportunity, we 
should stop ourselves form going to the lower re alms, because once we go there, as explained 
before, it is almost impossible to get out. Wh e n  w e  h a v e  t h i s  h u m a n  l i f e  o f  l e i s u r e  a n d  
opportunity, met the teachings and all the good co nditions are assembled together, the very least 
we can do is to close the door to the lower realms.   When we have been studying th e Dharma for some time, we may sometimes wish to listen to 
new teachings. Shantideva’s Engagi ng in the Bodhisattva Deeds is a text for practice. For students 
who have heard these teachings before, this is th e time to reflect and meditate on these points, 
especially for the senior students. (Geshe-la: Senior students should do senior things!)

3B2B 2B1A 2B2C  1 One deceives oneself if one does not make effort in virtue once one has 
obtained the leisures and endowments 
[4,23] 
So if, when having found leisure such as this, 
I do not attune myself to what is wholesome, 
There could be no greater deception 
And there could be no greater folly. 
 
This time, we have obtained this human life of leisure and opportunity, which is difficult to find 
and, once found, is able to fulfil the great purposes. We have met the teachings and the Mahayana virtuous friends. At such a time, if we do not use this opportunity to accomplish 
virtue but, instead, we spend our lives distracted  by the eight worldly dharmas, then our entire 
lives will be empty. If this happens, we have de ceived ourselves and there is no greater deception 
than this. There is no greater ignorance with rega rds to what is to be abandoned and what is to 
be cultivated. The point is that we have to be conscientious with regards to what is to be 
abandoned and what is to be cultivated. We should use this human life of leisure and 
opportunity to practise the holy Dharma. 
3B2B 2B1A 2B2C  2 One will  exp erience suffering in this life 
[4,24] 
And if, having understood this, 
I still foolishly continue to be slothful, 
When the hour of death arrives 
Tremendous grief will rear its head. 
 
“And if, having understood this,” in the first line of verse 24 refers to understanding   what has 
been said in the preceding verse. With such unde rstanding, if we still continue foolishly to be 
slothful, attracted to sense objects and continuous ly distracted, coming under the control of the 
eight worldly dharmas, then, at the time of death, there will be tremendous regret, grief, suffering 
and fear. Reflecting on this, we realise we need  to put great effort into cultivating virtue. 
3B2B 2B1A 2B2C  3 One will be tormented with th e suffering of the lower realms in the future 
[4,25] 
Then if my body blaz es for a long time

177 In the unbearable flames of hell, 
Inevitably my mind will be tormented 
By the fires of unendurable remorse 
 
Instead of practising virtue, we engage in non-virt ue or negativities all the time. In the future, we 
will be born in the unbearable hells where we have to stay for a long time. Our bodies will be roasted in the unbearable flames of hell and ment al suffering will torment our minds. Therefore, 
it is important to strive not to be st ained by any downfalls or negativities.  
 One can also apply this particular outline to the cultivation of conscientiousness with regards to 
bodhicitta and the trainings of th e bodhisattvas. If we do not want  to be tormented by suffering 
in hell, then we should strive to ensure that we  are not stained with the faults that come from 
degeneration of one’s bodhicitta.  One can also apply the previous point stated in  verse 24. We are now training in developing 
bodhicitta and the practices of the bodhisattvas. If  our bodhicitta or our training in the deeds of 
the bodhisattva degenerates, then, at the time of  death, we will experience tremendous grief, 
regret and so forth.

If now while able to discriminate

178 to being hypnotised by a spell. When one is hypn otised, one does not know what one is doing. If
